      <p><b>Northern Cyprus</b> (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">Kuzey Kıbrıs</i>), officially the <b>Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus</b> (<b>TRNC</b>; <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">Kuzey Kıbrıs Türk Cumhuriyeti</i>, <i>KKTC</i>), is a <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> state<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> that comprises the northeastern portion of the <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Cyprus" title="Geography of Cyprus">island of Cyprus</a>. <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">Recognised only</a> by <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, Northern Cyprus is considered by all other states to be part of the <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Republic of Cyprus</a>. </p>
      <p>Northern Cyprus extends from <a href="/wiki/Cape_Apostolos_Andreas" title="Cape Apostolos Andreas">the tip</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Karpass_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Karpass Peninsula">Karpass Peninsula</a> in the northeast to <a href="/wiki/Morphou_Bay" title="Morphou Bay">Morphou Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Kormakitis" title="Cape Kormakitis">Cape Kormakitis</a> and its westernmost point, the <a href="/wiki/Kokkina" title="Kokkina">Kokkina</a> <a href="/wiki/Exclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclave">exclave</a> in the west. Its southernmost point is the village of <a href="/wiki/Louroujina" title="Louroujina">Louroujina</a>. A <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Buffer_Zone_in_Cyprus" title="United Nations Buffer Zone in Cyprus">buffer zone</a> under the control of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> stretches between Northern Cyprus and the rest of the island and divides <a href="/wiki/Nicosia" title="Nicosia">Nicosia</a>, the island's largest city and capital of both sides. </p>
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/1974_Cypriot_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1974 Cypriot coup d'état">coup d'état in 1974</a>, performed as part of an attempt to annex the island to <a href="/wiki/Greek_military_junta_of_1967%E2%80%931974" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek military junta of 1967–1974">Greece</a>, prompted the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_invasion_of_Cyprus" title="Turkish invasion of Cyprus">Turkish invasion of Cyprus</a>. This resulted in the eviction of much of the north's <a href="/wiki/Greek_Cypriot" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Cypriot">Greek Cypriot</a> population, the flight of <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cypriots" title="Turkish Cypriots">Turkish Cypriots</a> from the south, and the partitioning of the island, leading to a unilateral declaration of independence by the north in 1983. Due to its lack of recognition, Northern Cyprus is heavily dependent on Turkey for economic, political and military support.<sup id="cite_ref-Agency2013_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agency2013-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Boas2012_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boas2012-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Navaro-Yashin2012_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Navaro-Yashin2012-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Attempts to reach a solution to the <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_dispute" title="Cyprus dispute">Cyprus dispute</a> have been unsuccessful. The <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Army">Turkish Army</a> maintains a <a href="/wiki/Turkish_military_forces_in_Northern_Cyprus" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish military forces in Northern Cyprus">large force</a> in Northern Cyprus. While its presence is supported and approved by the TRNC government, the Republic of Cyprus, the European Union as a whole, and the international community regard it as an occupation force, and its presence has been denounced in several <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_resolutions" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Security Council resolutions">United Nations Security Council resolutions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-9">[9]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Northern Cyprus is a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a>, democratic republic with a <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Northern_Cyprus" title="Culture of Northern Cyprus">cultural heritage</a> incorporating various influences and an <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Northern_Cyprus" title="Economy of Northern Cyprus">economy</a> that is dominated by the services sector. The economy has seen growth through the 2000s and 2010s, with the <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross national product">GNP</a> per capita more than tripling in the 2000s, but is held back by an <a href="/wiki/Embargo_against_Northern_Cyprus" title="Embargo against Northern Cyprus">international embargo</a> due to the official closure of the ports in Northern Cyprus by the Republic of Cyprus. The official language is <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Cypriot_Turkish" title="Cypriot Turkish">distinct local dialect</a> being spoken. The vast majority of the population consists of <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Muslims">Sunni Muslims</a>, while religious attitudes are mostly moderate and secular.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Northern Cyprus is an observer state of <a href="/wiki/Economic_Cooperation_Organization" title="Economic Cooperation Organization">ECO</a> and <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">OIC</a> under the title "<a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cypriot_State" title="Turkish Cypriot State">Turkish Cypriot State</a>", and of <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Assembly_of_the_Council_of_Europe" title="Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe">PACE</a> under the title "Turkish Cypriot Community". </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Cyprus" title="Ottoman Cyprus">Ottoman Cyprus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modern_history_of_Cyprus" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern history of Cyprus">Modern history of Cyprus</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span id="1960.E2.80.931974"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1960–1974">1960–1974</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Cypriot_intercommunal_violence" title="Cypriot intercommunal violence">Cypriot intercommunal violence</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Image_of_Faz%C4%B1l_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_in_1963.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Image_of_Faz%C4%B1l_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_in_1963.png/175px-Image_of_Faz%C4%B1l_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_in_1963.png" decoding="async" width="175" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Image_of_Faz%C4%B1l_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_in_1963.png/263px-Image_of_Faz%C4%B1l_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_in_1963.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/de/Image_of_Faz%C4%B1l_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_in_1963.png 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="466"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Image_of_Faz%C4%B1l_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_in_1963.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Faz%C4%B1l_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk" title="Fazıl Küçük">Fazıl Küçük</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cypriot" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Cypriot">Turkish Cypriot</a> leader and former Vice-President of <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_old_North_Nicosia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_old_North_Nicosia.jpg/220px-Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_old_North_Nicosia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_old_North_Nicosia.jpg/330px-Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_old_North_Nicosia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_old_North_Nicosia.jpg/440px-Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_old_North_Nicosia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6274" data-file-height="3639"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_old_North_Nicosia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_Square" title="Sarayönü Square">Sarayönü Square</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Nicosia" title="North Nicosia">North Nicosia</a> in 1969, after the division of the city
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A united Cyprus gained independence from British rule in August 1960, after both Greek and Turkish Cypriots agreed to abandon their respective plans for <i lang="el-Latn" title="Greek-language text"><a href="/wiki/Enosis" title="Enosis">enosis</a></i> (union with Greece) and <i lang="tr" title="Turkish-language text"><a href="/wiki/Taksim_(politics)" title="Taksim (politics)">taksim</a></i> (Turkish for "partition"). The agreement involved Cyprus being governed under a constitution which apportioned Cabinet posts, parliamentary seats and civil service jobs on an agreed ratio between the two communities. Within three years, tensions began to show between the Greek Cypriots and Turkish Cypriots in administrative affairs. In particular, disputes over separate municipalities and taxation created a deadlock in government. In 1963 <a href="/wiki/Makarios_III" title="Makarios III">President Makarios</a> proposed unilateral changes to the constitution, via <a href="/wiki/13_Amendments_proposed_by_Makarios_III" class="mw-redirect" title="13 Amendments proposed by Makarios III">13 amendments</a>. Turkey and the Turkish Cypriots rejected the proposed amendments, claiming that this was an attempt to settle constitutional disputes in favour of the Greek Cypriots<sup id="cite_ref-REJECTION_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-REJECTION-11">[11]</a></sup> and to demote Turkish status from co-founders of the state to one of minority status, removing their constitutional safeguards in the process. Turkish Cypriots filed a lawsuit against the 13 amendments in the Supreme Constitutional Court of Cyprus (SCCC). Makarios announced that he would not comply with the decision of the SCCC, whatever it was,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and defended his amendments as being necessary "to resolve constitutional deadlocks" as opposed to the stance of the SCCC.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 25 April 1963, the SCCC decided that Makarios's 13 amendments were illegal. The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Cyprus" title="Supreme Court of Cyprus">Cyprus Supreme Court</a>'s ruling found that Makarios had violated the constitution by failing to fully implement its measures and that Turkish Cypriots had not been allowed to return to their positions in government without first accepting the proposed constitutional amendments.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> On 21 May, the president of the SCCC resigned due to Makarios's stance. On 15 July, Makarios ignored the decision of the SCCC.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> After the resignation of the president of the SCCC, the SCCC ceased to exist. The Supreme Court of Cyprus (SCC) was formed by merging the SCCC and the High Court of Cyprus, and undertook the jurisdiction and powers of the SCCC and HCC.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> On 30 November, Makarios legalised the 13 proposals. In 1963, the Greek Cypriot wing of the government created the <a href="/wiki/Akritas_plan" title="Akritas plan">Akritas plan</a> which outlined a policy that would remove Turkish Cypriots from the government and ultimately lead to union with Greece. The plan stated that if the Turkish Cypriots objected then they should be "violently subjugated before foreign powers could intervene".<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 21 December 1963, shots were fired at a Turkish Cypriot crowd that had gathered as a Greek police patrol stopped two Turkish Cypriots, claiming to ask for identification; two Turkish Cypriots were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-solsten_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solsten-18">[18]</a></sup> Almost immediately, intercommunal violence broke out with a major Greek Cypriot paramilitary attack upon Turkish Cypriots in <a href="/wiki/Nicosia" title="Nicosia">Nicosia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Larnaca" title="Larnaca">Larnaca</a>. Though the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Resistance_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Resistance Organization">TMT</a>—a Turkish resistance group created in 1959 to promote a policy of <i lang="tr" title="Turkish-language text"><a href="/wiki/Taksim_(politics)" title="Taksim (politics)">taksim</a></i> (division or partition of Cyprus), in opposition to the Greek Cypriot nationalist group <a href="/wiki/EOKA" title="EOKA">EOKA</a> and its advocacy of <i lang="el-Latn" title="Greek-language text"><a href="/wiki/Enosis" title="Enosis">enosis</a></i> (union of Cyprus with Greece)—committed a number of acts of retaliation, historian of the Cyprus conflict <a href="/wiki/Keith_Kyle" title="Keith Kyle">Keith Kyle</a> noted that "there is no doubt that the main victims of the numerous incidents that took place during the next few months were Turks".<sup id="cite_ref-REJECTION_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-REJECTION-11">[11]</a></sup> Seven hundred Turkish hostages, including children, were taken from the northern suburbs of Nicosia. <a href="/wiki/Nikos_Sampson" title="Nikos Sampson">Nikos Sampson</a>, a nationalist and future coup leader, led a group of Greek Cypriot irregulars into the mixed suburb of <a href="/wiki/Omorphita" class="mw-redirect" title="Omorphita">Omorphita/Küçük Kaymaklı</a> and attacked the Turkish Cypriot population.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> By the end of 1964, 364 Turkish Cypriots and 174 Greek Cypriots had been killed.<sup id="cite_ref-oberling120_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oberling120-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Turkish Cypriot members of the government had by now withdrawn, creating an essentially Greek Cypriot administration in control of all institutions of the state. After the partnership government collapsed, the Greek Cypriot led administration was recognised as the legitimate government of the Republic of Cyprus at the stage of the debates in New York in February 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> In September 1964, the then <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretary_General" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Secretary General">United Nations Secretary General</a>, <a href="/wiki/U_Thant" title="U Thant">U Thant</a> reported that "UNFICYP carried out a detailed survey of all damage to properties throughout the island during the disturbances; it shows that in 109 villages, most of them Turkish-Cypriot or mixed villages, 527 houses have been destroyed while 2,000 others have suffered damage from looting".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Widespread looting of Turkish Cypriot villages prompted 20,000 refugees to retreat into <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cypriot_Enclaves" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Cypriot Enclaves">armed enclaves</a>, where they remained for the next 11 years,<sup id="cite_ref-HISTORY_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HISTORY-23">[23]</a></sup> relying on food and medical supplies from Turkey to survive. Turkish Cypriots formed paramilitary groups to defend the enclaves, leading to a gradual division of the island's communities into two hostile camps. The violence had also seen thousands of Turkish Cypriots attempt to escape the violence by emigrating to Britain, Australia and Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> On 28 December 1967, the Turkish Cypriot Provisional Administration was founded.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="1974.E2.80.931983"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1974–1983">1974–1983</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/1974_Cypriot_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1974 Cypriot coup d'état">1974 Cypriot coup d'état</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_invasion_of_Cyprus" title="Turkish invasion of Cyprus">Turkish invasion of Cyprus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Federated_State_of_Cyprus" title="Turkish Federated State of Cyprus">Turkish Federated State of Cyprus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rauf_Denktash.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Rauf_Denktash.jpg/175px-Rauf_Denktash.jpg" decoding="async" width="175" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Rauf_Denktash.jpg/263px-Rauf_Denktash.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Rauf_Denktash.jpg/350px-Rauf_Denktash.jpg 2x" data-file-width="493" data-file-height="640"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rauf_Denktash.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Rauf_Denkta%C5%9F" title="Rauf Denktaş">Rauf Denktaş</a>, founder and former President of the Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 6 July 1974, <a href="/wiki/Makarios_III" title="Makarios III">Makarios</a> accused the Greek government of turning the Cypriot National Guard into an army of occupation.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> On 15 July 1974, the <a href="/wiki/Greek_military_junta_of_1967%E2%80%9374" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek military junta of 1967–74">Greek military junta</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cypriot_National_Guard" title="Cypriot National Guard">Cypriot National Guard</a> backed a <a href="/wiki/1974_Cypriot_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1974 Cypriot coup d'état">Greek Cypriot military coup d'état</a> in Cyprus. Pro-<a href="/wiki/Enosis" title="Enosis">Enosis</a> <a href="/wiki/Nikos_Sampson" title="Nikos Sampson">Nikos Sampson</a> replaced President Makarios as the new president.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The Greek Cypriot coupists proclaimed the establishment of the "Hellenic Republic of Cyprus".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Turkey claimed that under the 1960 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Guarantee_(1960)" title="Treaty of Guarantee (1960)">Treaty of Guarantee</a>, the coup was sufficient reason for military action to protect the Turkish Cypriot populace, and thus <a href="/wiki/Turkish_invasion_of_Cyprus" title="Turkish invasion of Cyprus">Turkey invaded</a> Cyprus on 20 July. Turkish forces proceeded to take over the northern four-elevenths of the island (about 36% of Cyprus's total area). The coup caused a civil war filled with ethnic violence, after which it collapsed and Makarios returned to power.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>On 2 August 1975, in the negotiations in Vienna, a population exchange agreement was signed between community leaders <a href="/wiki/Rauf_Denkta%C5%9F" title="Rauf Denktaş">Rauf Denktaş</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glafcos_Clerides" title="Glafcos Clerides">Glafcos Clerides</a> under the auspices of United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-un.org_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un.org-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hakki2007_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hakki2007-31">[31]</a></sup> On the basis of the Agreement, 196,000 Greek Cypriots living in the north were exchanged for 42,000 Turkish Cypriots living in the south<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> (the number of settlers was disputed<sup id="cite_ref-BahcheliBartmann2004_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BahcheliBartmann2004-33">[33]</a></sup>). The Orthodox Greek Cypriots in <a href="/wiki/Rizokarpaso" title="Rizokarpaso">Rizokarpaso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ayios_Andronikos,_Cyprus" class="mw-redirect" title="Ayios Andronikos, Cyprus">Agios Andronikos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agia_Trias,_Cyprus" title="Agia Trias, Cyprus">Agia Triada</a> chose to stay in their villages,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> as did also Catholic <a href="/wiki/Maronites" title="Maronites">Maronites</a> in <a href="/wiki/Asomatos,_Kyrenia" title="Asomatos, Kyrenia">Asomatos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karpasia_(town)" title="Karpasia (town)">Karpasia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kormakitis" title="Kormakitis">Kormakitis</a>. Approximately 1,500 Greek Cypriots and 500 Turkish Cypriots remain missing.<sup id="cite_ref-FLEEING_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLEEING-35">[35]</a></sup> The invasion led to the formation of the first sovereign administrative body of Northern Cyprus in August 1974, the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Turkish_Cypriot_Administration" title="Autonomous Turkish Cypriot Administration">Autonomous Turkish Cypriot Administration</a>. </p>
      <p>In 1975, the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Federated_State_of_Cyprus" title="Turkish Federated State of Cyprus">Turkish Federated State of Cyprus</a> (<i lang="tr" title="Turkish-language text">Kıbrıs Türk Federe Devleti</i>) was declared as a first step towards a future federated Cypriot state, but was rejected by the Republic of Cyprus and the United Nations. </p>
      <p>The north unilaterally <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_the_Turkish_Republic_of_Northern_Cyprus" title="Declaration of Independence of the Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus">declared its independence</a> on 15 November 1983 under the name of the <i>Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Declaration_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Declaration-2">[2]</a></sup> This was rejected by the UN via <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_541" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 541">Security Council Resolution 541</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span id="1983.E2.80.93present"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1983–present">1983–present</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pro-TRNC_demonstration_in_Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_North_Nicosia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Pro-TRNC_demonstration_in_Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_North_Nicosia.jpg/220px-Pro-TRNC_demonstration_in_Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_North_Nicosia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Pro-TRNC_demonstration_in_Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_North_Nicosia.jpg/330px-Pro-TRNC_demonstration_in_Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_North_Nicosia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Pro-TRNC_demonstration_in_Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_North_Nicosia.jpg/440px-Pro-TRNC_demonstration_in_Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_North_Nicosia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pro-TRNC_demonstration_in_Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_North_Nicosia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Saray%C3%B6n%C3%BC_Square" title="Sarayönü Square">Atatürk Square</a>, North Nicosia in 2006, with the Northern Cyprus and Turkish flags.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In recent years, the politics of reunification has dominated the island's affairs. The European Union decided in 2000 to accept Cyprus as a member, even if it was divided. This was due to their view of <a href="/wiki/Rauf_Denkta%C5%9F" title="Rauf Denktaş">Rauf Denktaş</a>, the pro-independence Turkish Cypriot President, as the main stumbling block, but also due to Greece threatening to block eastern EU expansion. It was hoped that Cyprus's planned accession into the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> would act as a catalyst towards a settlement. In the time leading up to Cyprus becoming a member, a new government was elected in Turkey and Rauf Denktaş lost political power in Cyprus. In 2004, a United Nations–brokered peace settlement was presented in a <a href="/wiki/Cypriot_Annan_Plan_referendums,_2004" class="mw-redirect" title="Cypriot Annan Plan referendums, 2004">referendum</a> to both sides.<sup id="cite_ref-Immovable_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immovable-36">[36]</a></sup> The proposed settlement was opposed by both the president of Cyprus, <a href="/wiki/Tassos_Papadopoulos" title="Tassos Papadopoulos">Tassos Papadopoulos</a>, and Turkish Cypriot president <a href="/wiki/Rauf_Denkta%C5%9F" title="Rauf Denktaş">Rauf Denktaş</a>; in the referendum, while 65% of Turkish Cypriots accepted the proposal, 76% of Greek Cypriots rejected it. As a result, Cyprus entered the European Union divided, with the <a href="/wiki/Community_acquis" class="mw-redirect" title="Community acquis">effects of membership</a> suspended for Northern Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-Immovable_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immovable-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Denktaş resigned in the wake of the vote, ushering in the pro-settlement <a href="/wiki/Mehmet_Ali_Talat" title="Mehmet Ali Talat">Mehmet Ali Talat</a> as his successor. However, the pro-settlement side and Mehmet Ali Talat lost momentum due to the ongoing embargo and isolation,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> despite promises from the European Union that these would be eased.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> As a result, the Turkish Cypriot electorate became frustrated. This led ultimately to the pro-independence side winning the general elections in 2009 and its candidate, former Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Dervi%C5%9F_Ero%C4%9Flu" title="Derviş Eroğlu">Derviş Eroğlu</a>, winning the presidential elections in 2010. Although Eroğlu and his <a href="/wiki/National_Unity_Party_(Northern_Cyprus)" title="National Unity Party (Northern Cyprus)">National Unity Party</a> favours the independence of Northern Cyprus rather than reunification with the Republic of Cyprus, he is negotiating with the Greek Cypriot side towards a settlement for reunification.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2011, Turkish Cypriots protested against economic reforms made by the Northern Cyprus and Turkish governments; <i>see <a href="/wiki/2011_Turkish_Cypriot_demonstrations" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Turkish Cypriot demonstrations">2011 Turkish Cypriot demonstrations</a></i>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Northern_Cyprus" title="Districts of Northern Cyprus">Districts of Northern Cyprus</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Northern Cyprus is divided into six districts: <a href="/wiki/Lefko%C5%9Fa_District" title="Lefkoşa District">Lefkoşa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gazima%C4%9Fusa_District" title="Gazimağusa District">Gazimağusa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrenia_District" title="Kyrenia District">Girne</a>, <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCzelyurt_District" title="Güzelyurt District">Güzelyurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0skele_District" title="İskele District">İskele</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lefke_District" title="Lefke District">Lefke</a>. Lefke District was established by separation from the Güzelyurt District in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In addition there are further twelve sub-districts divided between the five larger districts and twenty-eight municipalities. </p> 
      <div style="position: relative">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Blank_district_map_Northern_Cyprus.png" class="image" title="Blank district map of Northern Cyprus"><img alt="Blank district map of Northern Cyprus" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Blank_district_map_Northern_Cyprus.png/600px-Blank_district_map_Northern_Cyprus.png" decoding="async" width="600" height="384" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Blank_district_map_Northern_Cyprus.png/900px-Blank_district_map_Northern_Cyprus.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Blank_district_map_Northern_Cyprus.png/1200px-Blank_district_map_Northern_Cyprus.png 2x" data-file-width="1852" data-file-height="1184"></a> 
       <div style="position:absolute;left:220px;top:200px;">
        <small><a href="/wiki/Lefko%C5%9Fa_District" title="Lefkoşa District">Lefkoşa</a></small>
       </div> 
       <div style="position:absolute;left:165px;top:165px;">
        <small><a href="/wiki/Kyrenia_District" title="Kyrenia District">Girne</a></small>
       </div> 
       <div style="position:absolute;left:410px;top:120px;">
        <small><a href="/wiki/%C4%B0skele_District" title="İskele District">İskele</a></small>
       </div> 
       <div style="position:absolute;left:95px;top:200px;">
        <small><a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCzelyurt_District" title="Güzelyurt District">Güzelyurt</a></small>
       </div> 
       <div style="position:absolute;left:295px;top:200px;">
        <small><a href="/wiki/Gazima%C4%9Fusa_District" title="Gazimağusa District">Gazimağusa</a></small>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Northern_Cyprus" title="Politics of Northern Cyprus">Politics of Northern Cyprus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ersin_Tatar_in_2019.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Ersin_Tatar_in_2019.png/220px-Ersin_Tatar_in_2019.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="304" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/77/Ersin_Tatar_in_2019.png 1.5x" data-file-width="275" data-file-height="380"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ersin_Tatar_in_2019.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ersin_Tatar" title="Ersin Tatar">Ersin Tatar</a>, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Northern_Cyprus" title="President of Northern Cyprus">President of Northern Cyprus</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The politics of Northern Cyprus takes place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>, whereby the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Northern_Cyprus" title="President of Northern Cyprus">President</a> is <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and of a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">government</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_Republic_of_Northern_Cyprus" class="mw-redirect" title="Assembly of the Republic of Northern Cyprus">Assembly of the Republic</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Northern_Cyprus" title="Judiciary of Northern Cyprus">Judiciary</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature. </p>
      <p>The president is elected for a five-year term and is currently <a href="/wiki/Ersin_Tatar" title="Ersin Tatar">Ersin Tatar</a>. The current Prime Minister is Ersan Saner. The legislature is the Assembly of the Republic, which has 50 members elected by <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> from six electoral districts. In the elections of January 2018, the right-wing <a href="/wiki/National_Unity_Party_(Northern_Cyprus)" title="National Unity Party (Northern Cyprus)">National Unity Party</a> won the most seats in the Assembly, and the current government is a coalition of the National Unity Party and the centrist <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Northern_Cyprus)" title="People's Party (Northern Cyprus)">People's Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Due to Northern Cyprus's isolation and heavy reliance on Turkish support, Turkey has a high level of influence over the country's politics. This has led to some experts characterising it as an effective <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">puppet state</a> of Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-Kurtulus2005_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kurtulus2005-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Focarelli2012_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Focarelli2012-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PanaraWilson2013_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PanaraWilson2013-44">[44]</a></sup> Other experts, however, have pointed out to the independent nature of elections and appointments in Northern Cyprus and disputes between the Turkish Cypriot and Turkish governments, concluding that "puppet state" is not an accurate description for Northern Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_status_and_foreign_relations">International status and foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Northern_Cyprus" title="Foreign relations of Northern Cyprus">Foreign relations of Northern Cyprus</a>
      </div>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
