         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_Turkish_Cypriot_Leader_Akinci_in_New_York_City_(21901946901).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Ak%C4%B1nc%C4%B1" title="Mustafa Akıncı">Mustafa Akıncı</a> with U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>, 2 October 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>No nation other than Turkey<sup id="cite_ref-Kurtulus2005_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kurtulus2005-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Commerce2003_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commerce2003-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIA_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-49">[49]</a></sup> has officially recognised Northern Cyprus as a sovereign state. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> recognises it as territory of the Republic of Cyprus under Turkish occupation.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_Security_Council_Resolution_550_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Security_Council_Resolution_550-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Leckie2007_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leckie2007-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Quigley_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quigley-52">[52]</a></sup> Pakistan and Bangladesh had initially declared their recognition of Northern Cyprus as a sovereign state shortly after its declaration of independence,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> but they withdrew their recognition as a result of US pressure after the UN deemed the declaration illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The United Nations considers the declaration of independence by Northern Cyprus as legally invalid, as enunciated in several of its resolutions.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_Security_Council_Resolution_550_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Security_Council_Resolution_550-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNSCR541_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNSCR541-55">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the wake of the April 2004 referendum on the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Annan_Plan_for_Cyprus" class="mw-redirect" title="Annan Plan for Cyprus">Annan Plan</a>, and in view of the support of the Turkish Cypriot community for the plan, the European Union made pledges towards ending the isolation of Northern Cyprus. These included measures for trade and €259 million in aid.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A pledge by the EU to lift the embargo on Northern Cyprus in the wake of the Annan Plan referendums has been blocked by the Greek Cypriot government.<sup id="cite_ref-Immovable_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immovable-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Co-operation</a> upgraded the delegation of the Turkish Cypriot Muslim community from "observer community" (1979) to that of a <a href="/wiki/Constituent_state" title="Constituent state">constituent state</a> with the designation "<a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cypriot_State" title="Turkish Cypriot State">Turkish Cypriot State</a>", making Northern Cyprus an observer member of the organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-OIC_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OIC-56">[56]</a></sup> A number of high-profile formal meetings have also taken place between Turkish Cypriot presidents and various foreign leaders and politicians. </p>
      <p>In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Assembly_of_the_Council_of_Europe" title="Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe">Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe</a> gave observer status to the representatives of Turkish Cypriot community.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Since then, Northern Cyprus's representatives have actively participated in all PACE activities without voting rights. </p>
      <p>The European Union considers the area not under effective control of the Republic of Cyprus as EU territory under Turkish military occupation and thus indefinitely exempt from <a href="/wiki/Community_acquis" class="mw-redirect" title="Community acquis">EU legislation</a> until a settlement has been found. The status of Northern Cyprus has become a recurrent issue especially during the recent talks for <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Turkey_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Turkey to the European Union">Turkey's membership of the EU</a> where the division of the island is seen as a major stumbling block in Turkey's road to membership.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Autonomous Republic of <a href="/wiki/Nakhichivan_Autonomous_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Nakhichivan Autonomous Republic">Nakhichevan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> has issued a resolution recognising the independence of Northern Cyprus. As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a> issue, however, Azerbaijan itself has not recognised North Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Turkish Cypriots have been applying for decades for passports issued by <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>. When the entry points with the Republic of Cyprus were closed, the applications were made either through middlemen or through consulates and embassies of Cyprus in other countries. A yearly increase in the number of applications for such passports of 10–15% was observed in years prior to 2001, when the rate greatly increased and 817 were issued in the first eight months of 2001 as compared to 448 for the whole of 2000. After the opening of the borders with the Republic of Cyprus, Turkish Cypriots started line-ups applying for Cypriot passports by visiting the Republic of Cyprus and showing proof of their Cypriot ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-Navaro-Yashin2012No2_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Navaro-Yashin2012No2-61">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are seven border crossings between Northern Cyprus and the Republic of Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Since May 2004 some tourists have taken to flying to the Republic of Cyprus directly then crossing the green line to holiday in Northern Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (January 2015)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>On 21 September 2011, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and Northern Cyprus signed an EEZ border agreement in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 2012, Northern Cyprus became an observer member of the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Cooperation_Organization" title="Economic Cooperation Organization">Economic Cooperation Organization</a> under the name "Turkish Cypriot State". </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Security_Forces_Command" title="Security Forces Command">Security Forces Command</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Northern_Cyprus_Republic_Day_parade_2007_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Northern_Cyprus_Republic_Day_parade_2007_2.JPG/220px-Northern_Cyprus_Republic_Day_parade_2007_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Northern_Cyprus_Republic_Day_parade_2007_2.JPG/330px-Northern_Cyprus_Republic_Day_parade_2007_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Northern_Cyprus_Republic_Day_parade_2007_2.JPG/440px-Northern_Cyprus_Republic_Day_parade_2007_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3064" data-file-height="1863"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Northern_Cyprus_Republic_Day_parade_2007_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cypriot" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Cypriot">Turkish Cypriot</a> soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/Security_Forces_Command" title="Security Forces Command">Security Forces Command</a> perform during a Republic Day parade.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Security Forces Command consists of an 8,000 strong force primarily made up of conscripted Turkish Cypriot males between the ages of 18 and 40.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> There is also an additional reserve force which consists of about 10,000 first-line and 16,000 second-line troops conscripted up to the age of 50. The <a href="/wiki/Security_Forces_Command" title="Security Forces Command">Security Forces Command</a> is lightly armed and heavily dependent on its mainland Turkish allies, from which it draws much of its officer corps.<sup id="cite_ref-SolstenDivision1993_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SolstenDivision1993-66">[66]</a></sup> It is led by a Brigadier General drawn from the Turkish Army. It acts essentially as a <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">gendarmerie</a> charged with protection of the border of Northern Cyprus from Greek Cypriot incursions and maintaining internal security within Northern Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-janes_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-janes-67">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In addition, the mainland <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Armed_Forces" title="Turkish Armed Forces">Turkish Armed Forces</a> maintains the <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_Turkish_Peace_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyprus Turkish Peace Force">Cyprus Turkish Peace Force</a> which consists of around 30,000–40,000 troops drawn from the 9th Turkish Army Corps and comprising two divisions, the 28th and 39th. It is equipped with a substantial number of <a href="/wiki/US" class="mw-redirect" title="US">US</a>-made <a href="/wiki/M48_Patton#Turkish_variants" title="M48 Patton">M48 Patton</a> <a href="/wiki/Main_battle_tanks" class="mw-redirect" title="Main battle tanks">main battle tanks</a> and artillery weapons. The <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Air_Force" title="Turkish Air Force">Turkish Air Force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Navy">Turkish Navy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Coast_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Coast Guard">Turkish Coast Guard</a> also have a presence in Northern Cyprus. Although formally part of Turkish 4th Army, headquartered in İzmir, the sensitivities of the Cyprus situation means that the commander of the <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_Turkish_Peace_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyprus Turkish Peace Force">Cyprus Turkish Peace Force</a> also reports directly to the Turkish General Staff in <a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_Turkish_Peace_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyprus Turkish Peace Force">Cyprus Turkish Peace Force</a> is deployed principally along the <a href="/wiki/Green_Line_(Cyprus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Line (Cyprus)">Green Line</a> and in locations where hostile amphibious landings might take place.<sup id="cite_ref-janes_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-janes-67">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The presence of the mainland Turkish military in Cyprus is highly controversial, having been denounced as an occupation force by the Republic of Cyprus and the international community. Several <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> resolutions have called on the Turkish forces to withdraw.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-9">[9]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Northern_Cyprus" title="Human rights in Northern Cyprus">Human rights in Northern Cyprus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nicosia_01-2017_img33_AtatuerkSquare.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Nicosia_01-2017_img33_AtatuerkSquare.jpg/220px-Nicosia_01-2017_img33_AtatuerkSquare.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Nicosia_01-2017_img33_AtatuerkSquare.jpg/330px-Nicosia_01-2017_img33_AtatuerkSquare.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Nicosia_01-2017_img33_AtatuerkSquare.jpg/440px-Nicosia_01-2017_img33_AtatuerkSquare.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4754" data-file-height="2971"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nicosia_01-2017_img33_AtatuerkSquare.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The law courts building in <a href="/wiki/North_Nicosia" title="North Nicosia">North Nicosia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In January 2011, <i>The Report of the Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights on the question of Human Rights in Cyprus</i> noted that the ongoing division of Cyprus continues to affect human rights throughout the island "...&nbsp;including freedom of movement, human rights pertaining to the question of missing persons, discrimination, the right to life, freedom of religion, and economic, social and cultural rights."<sup id="cite_ref-ohchr_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohchr-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> has classified the perceived level of democratic and political freedom in Northern Cyprus as "free" since 2000 in its <i><a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World_(report)" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom in the World (report)">Freedom in the World</a></i> report.<sup id="cite_ref-freeh_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freeh-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The 2016 ranking was "free" with the scores (1: most free, 7: least free) political rights: 2/7, civil liberties: 2/7 and aggregate score: 79/100.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>' World Press Freedom Index ranked Northern Cyprus 76th among 180 countries in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Enclaved_Greek_Cypriots" class="mw-redirect" title="Enclaved Greek Cypriots">Greek Cypriot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maronite_Cypriots" title="Maronite Cypriots">Maronite</a> communities, numbering 343 and 118 respectively as of 2014, are denied the right to vote in presidential, parliamentary and municipal elections or run for office. Maronites do elect <a href="/wiki/Mukhtar" title="Mukhtar">the leader of their village</a>, whilst Greek Cypriots have two appointed leaders, one by the Turkish Cypriot government and the other by the Republic of Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-tchrf_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tchrf-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>World Happiness Report 2016 of United Nations' Sustainable Development Solutions Network (SDSN) ranked Northern Cyprus 62nd among 157 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Gallup Healthways Well-Being Index of 2014 ranked Northern Cyprus 49th among 145 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Northern Cyprus received 153 asylum applications during 2011–14 according to United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees (UNHCR).<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Cyprus" title="Geography of Cyprus">Geography of Cyprus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Cyprus" title="Climate of Cyprus">Climate of Cyprus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:1002px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Morphou_Bay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Morphou_Bay.jpg/1000px-Morphou_Bay.jpg" decoding="async" width="1000" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Morphou_Bay.jpg/1500px-Morphou_Bay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Morphou_Bay.jpg/2000px-Morphou_Bay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10626" data-file-height="1617"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Morphou_Bay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div>Panoramic view of the <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCzelyurt_District" title="Güzelyurt District">Güzelyurt District</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morphou_Bay" title="Morphou Bay">Morphou Bay</a> as seen from the <a href="/wiki/Troodos_Mountains" title="Troodos Mountains">Troodos mountains</a>.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Northern Cyprus has an area of 3,355 square kilometres (1,295&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), which amounts to around a third of the island. 75 kilometres (47&nbsp;mi) to the north of Northern Cyprus lies <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> with <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> lying 97 kilometres (60.3&nbsp;mi) to the east. It lies between latitudes 34° and 36° N, and longitudes 32° and 35° E. </p>
      <p>The coastline of Northern Cyprus features two bays: the <a href="/wiki/Morphou_Bay" title="Morphou Bay">Morphou Bay</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Famagusta_Bay" title="Famagusta Bay">Famagusta Bay</a>, and there are four capes: <a href="/wiki/Cape_Apostolos_Andreas" title="Cape Apostolos Andreas">Cape Apostolos Andreas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Kormakitis" title="Cape Kormakitis">Cape Kormakitis</a>, Cape Zeytin and Cape Kasa, with Cape Apostolos Andreas being the endpoint of the <a href="/wiki/Karpaz_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Karpaz Peninsula">Karpaz Peninsula</a>. The narrow <a href="/wiki/Kyrenia_Mountains" title="Kyrenia Mountains">Kyrenia mountain range</a> lies along the northern coastline, and the highest point in Northern Cyprus, Mount Selvili, lies in this mountain range with an altitude of 1,024 metres (3,360&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mesaoria" title="Mesaoria">Mesaoria</a> plain, extending from the <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCzelyurt_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Güzelyurt district">Güzelyurt district</a> to the eastern coastline is another defining landscape. The Mesaoria plains consist of plain fields and small hills, and is crossed by several seasonal streams. The eastern part of the plain is used for dry agriculture, such as the cultivation of wheat and barley, and are therefore predominantly green in the winter and spring, while it turns yellow and brown in the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>56.7% of the land in Northern Cyprus is agriculturally viable.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Wild_donkeys_on_Cyprus.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Wild_donkeys_on_Cyprus.JPG/220px-Wild_donkeys_on_Cyprus.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Wild_donkeys_on_Cyprus.JPG/330px-Wild_donkeys_on_Cyprus.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Wild_donkeys_on_Cyprus.JPG/440px-Wild_donkeys_on_Cyprus.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4188" data-file-height="3066"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wild_donkeys_on_Cyprus.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Wild Cyprus donkeys inhabit the mainly remote northern region of the <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0skele_District" title="İskele District">İskele District</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A relatively unspoiled part of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a> <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">biodiversity hotspot</a>, Northern Cyprus has considerable ecological diversity, containing a variety of terrestrial <a href="/wiki/Habitat" title="Habitat">habitats</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Its flora includes around 1900 plant species, of which 19 are endemic to Northern Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-metuf_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metuf-82">[82]</a></sup> Even in the urban areas, there is a lot of diversity: a study conducted on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Pedieos" title="Pedieos">Pedieos</a> river around Nicosia found more than 750 different plant species.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Among these species are 30 of the orchid species that are endemic to Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-metuf_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metuf-82">[82]</a></sup> An endangered species that is the subject of folk tales and myths is the <a href="/wiki/Pancratium_maritimum" title="Pancratium maritimum">sea daffodil</a>, found on the sandy beaches and endangered due to the disruption of their habitats.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The medoş tulip (<i><a href="/wiki/Tulipa_cypria" title="Tulipa cypria">Tulipa cypria</a></i>) is a notable species that is endemic to Northern Cyprus; it is only found in the villages of <a href="/wiki/Diorios" title="Diorios">Tepebaşı/Diorios</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ayios_Symeon" class="mw-redirect" title="Ayios Symeon">Avtepe/Ayios Simeon</a>, and is celebrated with an annual festival.<sup id="cite_ref-flouna_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flouna-85">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the national park in the <a href="/wiki/Karpaz_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Karpaz Peninsula">Karpaz Peninsula</a> around <a href="/wiki/Cape_Apostolos_Andreas" title="Cape Apostolos Andreas">Cape Apostolos Andreas</a>, there is a population of around 1,000 wild <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_donkey" title="Cyprus donkey">Cyprus donkeys</a>. These donkeys, under the protection of the Turkish Cypriot government, are free to wander in herds over an area of 300 square kilometres (120 <a href="/wiki/Square_mile" title="Square mile">square miles</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The donkeys have earned a strong image for the peninsula, which is also home to a rich fauna and relatively big forests.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The beaches of Northern Cyprus also include sites where hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Loggerhead_turtle" class="mw-redirect" title="Loggerhead turtle">loggerhead turtles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Green_turtle" class="mw-redirect" title="Green turtle">green turtles</a> lay eggs, which hatch at the end of the summer, followed by observers.<sup id="cite_ref-flouna_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flouna-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Morning_beach_near_Mehmetcik_(North_Cyprus)_2003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Morning_beach_near_Mehmetcik_%28North_Cyprus%29_2003.jpg/220px-Morning_beach_near_Mehmetcik_%28North_Cyprus%29_2003.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Morning_beach_near_Mehmetcik_%28North_Cyprus%29_2003.jpg/330px-Morning_beach_near_Mehmetcik_%28North_Cyprus%29_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Morning_beach_near_Mehmetcik_%28North_Cyprus%29_2003.jpg/440px-Morning_beach_near_Mehmetcik_%28North_Cyprus%29_2003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1984" data-file-height="1312"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Morning_beach_near_Mehmetcik_(North_Cyprus)_2003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Beach near <a href="/wiki/Galateia" title="Galateia">Mehmetcik</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0skele_District" title="İskele District">İskele District</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The winter in Northern Cyprus is cool and rainy, particularly between December and February, with 60% of annual rainfall.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> These rains produce winter torrents that fill most of the rivers, which typically dry up as the year progresses. Snow has been known to fall on the Kyrenia Range, but seldom elsewhere in spite of low night temperatures. The short spring is characterised by unstable weather, occasional heavy storms and the "meltem", or westerly wind. Summer is hot and dry enough to turn low-lying lands on the island brown. Parts of the island experience the "Poyraz", a north-westerly wind, or the <a href="/wiki/Sirocco" title="Sirocco">sirocco</a>, a wind from Africa, which is dry and dusty. Summer is followed by a short, turbulent autumn. </p>
      <p>Climate conditions on the island vary by geographical factors. The Mesaoria Plain, cut off from the summer breezes and from much of the humidity of the sea, may reach temperature peaks of 40 to 45&nbsp;°C (104 to 113&nbsp;°F). Humidity rises at the Karpaz Peninsula. Humidity and water temperature, 16 to 28&nbsp;°C (61 to 82&nbsp;°F), combine to stabilise coastal weather, which does not experience inland extremes. The Southern Range blocks air currents that bring rain and atmospheric humidity from the south-west, diminishing both on its eastern side. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Northern_Cyprus" title="Economy of Northern Cyprus">Economy of Northern Cyprus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrenia_01-2017_img04_view_from_castle_bastion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Kyrenia_01-2017_img04_view_from_castle_bastion.jpg/220px-Kyrenia_01-2017_img04_view_from_castle_bastion.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Kyrenia_01-2017_img04_view_from_castle_bastion.jpg/330px-Kyrenia_01-2017_img04_view_from_castle_bastion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Kyrenia_01-2017_img04_view_from_castle_bastion.jpg/440px-Kyrenia_01-2017_img04_view_from_castle_bastion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4582" data-file-height="2864"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrenia_01-2017_img04_view_from_castle_bastion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kyrenia" title="Kyrenia">Kyrenia</a> (Girne) is one of the main tourist resorts in Northern Cyprus. Tourism is one of the dominant sectors of the Northern Cyprus' economy.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The economy of Northern Cyprus is dominated by the services sector (69% of GDP in 2007) which includes the public sector, trade, tourism and education. The revenues gained by the education sector in 2011 was $400 million.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Industry (light manufacturing) contributes 22% of GDP and agriculture 9%.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-90">[90]</a></sup> The economy of Northern Cyprus is based on a <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a> approach<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> and it became the top country in Europe in entrepreneurial intent to start a new business in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Economic development is adversely affected by the continuing Cyprus problem. Northern Cyprus is under an <a href="/wiki/Embargo_against_Northern_Cyprus" title="Embargo against Northern Cyprus">international embargo</a> as the Republic of Cyprus, as the internationally recognised authority, has declared airports and ports in the area not under its effective control closed. All UN member states other than Turkey respect the closure of those ports and airports.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> As a result, Northern Cyprus is heavily dependent on Turkish economic support,<sup id="cite_ref-indepuni_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indepuni-94">[94]</a></sup> and is still dependent on monetary transfers from the Turkish government.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Northern Cyprus uses the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Lira" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Lira">Turkish Lira</a> as its currency which links its economy to that of Turkey's. Since the Republic of Cyprus joined the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euro</a> zone and the movement of peoples between the north and south has become more free, the Euro is also in wide circulation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Exports and imports have to go via Turkey;<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> while European Union promised an opening up of the ports after the Annan plan, this was blocked by the Republic of Cyprus and exporting through the south, while technically possible, remains impractical.<sup id="cite_ref-bryant_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bryant-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Despite the constraints imposed by the lack of international recognition, the nominal GDP growth rates of the economy in 2001–2005 were 5.4%, 6.9%, 11.4%, 15.4% and 10.6%, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Oxford_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxford-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unistar_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unistar-98">[98]</a></sup> The real GDP growth rate in 2007 was estimated at 2%.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-90">[90]</a></sup> This growth has been buoyed by the relative stability of the Turkish Lira and a boom in the education and construction sectors. Between 2002 and 2007, <a href="/wiki/Gross_National_Product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross National Product">Gross National Product</a> per capita more than tripled, from US$4,409 in 2002 to US$16,158 (in current U.S. dollars).<sup id="cite_ref-yb2006_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yb2006-99">[99]</a></sup> The growth continued through the 2010s, with real growth rates of 3.7%, 3.9%, 1.8% and 1.1% respectively in 2010–2013.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The unemployment rate declined through the 2010s and was at 8.3% in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2011, North Cyprus sold electricity to the Republic of Cyprus following an <a href="/wiki/Evangelos_Florakis_Naval_Base_explosion" title="Evangelos Florakis Naval Base explosion">explosion</a> in the southern part of the island which affected a large power station.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Cyprus_Water_Supply_Project" title="Northern Cyprus Water Supply Project">Northern Cyprus Water Supply Project</a>, completed in 2015, is aimed at delivering water for drinking and irrigation from southern Turkey via a pipeline under the Mediterranean Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-dsi_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dsi-103">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>International telephone calls are routed via a Turkish <a href="/wiki/Country_calling_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Country calling code">dialling code</a> (<a href="/wiki/%2B90" class="mw-redirect" title="+90">+90 392</a>) as Northern Cyprus has neither its own country code nor official <a href="/wiki/ITU_prefix" title="ITU prefix">ITU prefix</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Similarly with the internet Northern Cyprus has no <a href="/wiki/CcTLD" class="mw-redirect" title="CcTLD">top level domain</a> of its own and is under the Turkish second-level domain <a href="/wiki/.nc.tr" class="mw-redirect" title=".nc.tr">.nc.tr</a>. Items of mail must be addressed 'via Mersin 10, TURKEY' as the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Postal_Union" title="Universal Postal Union">Universal Postal Union</a> does not recognise Northern Cyprus as a separate entity.<sup id="cite_ref-Office2010_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office2010-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Maric2009_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maric2009-105">[105]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio" title="Amateur radio">Amateur radio</a> operators sometimes use <a href="/wiki/Callsign" class="mw-redirect" title="Callsign">callsigns</a> beginning with "1B", but these have no standing for awards or other operating credit. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Northern_Cyprus" title="Tourism in Northern Cyprus">Tourism in Northern Cyprus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:1092px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrenia_Harbour_Panorama,_North_Cyprus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Kyrenia_Harbour_Panorama%2C_North_Cyprus.jpg/1090px-Kyrenia_Harbour_Panorama%2C_North_Cyprus.jpg" decoding="async" width="1090" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Kyrenia_Harbour_Panorama%2C_North_Cyprus.jpg/1635px-Kyrenia_Harbour_Panorama%2C_North_Cyprus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Kyrenia_Harbour_Panorama%2C_North_Cyprus.jpg/2180px-Kyrenia_Harbour_Panorama%2C_North_Cyprus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5083" data-file-height="942"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Kyrenia_Harbour_Panorama,_North_Cyprus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div>Panoramic view of the Kyrenia Harbour, with the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venetian</a>-era <a href="/wiki/Kyrenia_Castle" title="Kyrenia Castle">Kyrenia Castle</a> on the far left, and the <a href="/wiki/Kyrenia_Mountains" title="Kyrenia Mountains">Kyrenia Mountains</a> in the background
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tourism is considered as one of the driving sectors of the Turkish Cypriot economy. The country received over 1.1 million tourists in 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-turanket_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turanket-106">[106]</a></sup> when hotels and restaurants generated an income of $328 million<sup id="cite_ref-secgdp_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-secgdp-107">[107]</a></sup> and constituted 8.5% of the GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Accommodation and catering created more than 10,000 jobs in the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The tourism sector has seen great development in the 2000s and 2010s, with the number of tourists more than doubling, increased investment and hotel construction; official estimates of income derived from tourism were around 700 million US dollars in 2013 and the total bed capacity was estimated to be around 20,000.<sup id="cite_ref-tgbakan_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tgbakan-110">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Casino_in_Girne_(Nord-Cypern)_2003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Casino_in_Girne_%28Nord-Cypern%29_2003.jpg/220px-Casino_in_Girne_%28Nord-Cypern%29_2003.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Casino_in_Girne_%28Nord-Cypern%29_2003.jpg/330px-Casino_in_Girne_%28Nord-Cypern%29_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Casino_in_Girne_%28Nord-Cypern%29_2003.jpg/440px-Casino_in_Girne_%28Nord-Cypern%29_2003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1984" data-file-height="1312"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Casino_in_Girne_(Nord-Cypern)_2003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Casino tourism is one of the major sectors of the North Cyprus economy.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kyrenia is considered the capital of tourism in Northern Cyprus, with its numerous hotels, entertainment facilities, vibrant nightlife and shopping areas.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> In 2012, 62.7% of the visitors in Northern Cyprus stayed in the <a href="/wiki/Girne_District" title="Girne District">Girne District</a> during their visit.<sup id="cite_ref-turanket_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turanket-106">[106]</a></sup> Out of the 145 hotels in Northern Cyprus, 99 were in the Girne District in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-tgbakan_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tgbakan-110">[110]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Northern Cyprus has traditionally been an attraction for beach holidays, partly thanks to its reputation as an unspoiled area. Its mild climate, rich history and nature are seen as sources of attraction. A significant sector of <a href="/wiki/Eco-tourism" class="mw-redirect" title="Eco-tourism">eco-tourism</a> has been developed in Northern Cyprus, as tourists visit it for bird watching, cycling, walking and observing flowers in the wild. It is praised for its relative safety, and especially for the <a href="/wiki/Karpass_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Karpass Peninsula">Karpass Peninsula</a>, its well-preservation.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> The peninsula is home to several sorts of tourism: it hosts the <a href="/wiki/Vokolida" title="Vokolida">Bafra</a> Tourism Area as a center for beach-goers, where four luxurious and large hotels were built until 2014, several facilities and regular festivals that highlight its rural qualities and exhibit local traditions, a remote natural park, the <a href="/wiki/Kantara_Castle" title="Kantara Castle">Kantara Castle</a> attracting sightseers, and a marina that was built to host international yachts and boats, along with large facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Casino tourism has also grown to become a significant contribution to the economy in Northern Cyprus. They were first opened in the 1990s, and have since become very popular with visitors from Turkey and the rest of the island, where casinos are banned. This has led to huge investments in the casino sector.<sup id="cite_ref-ertr_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ertr-114">[114]</a></sup> However, the sector has been criticised due to claims of its lack of benefits for the small and middle-scale business and shop owners.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> The "nightclubs" that have been established for <a href="/wiki/Prostitution" title="Prostitution">prostitution</a> attract <a href="/wiki/Sex_tourism" title="Sex tourism">sex tourism</a> to Northern Cyprus and the industry has been described as a "civilized one", despite the sex workers being described as "vulnerable to abuse".<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure<span class="anchor" id="Communications_and_transport"></span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ercan_Airport_North_Cyprus_005.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Ercan_Airport_North_Cyprus_005.JPG/220px-Ercan_Airport_North_Cyprus_005.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Ercan_Airport_North_Cyprus_005.JPG/330px-Ercan_Airport_North_Cyprus_005.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Ercan_Airport_North_Cyprus_005.JPG/440px-Ercan_Airport_North_Cyprus_005.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ercan_Airport_North_Cyprus_005.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Ercan_International_Airport" title="Ercan International Airport">Ercan International Airport</a> serves as the main port of entry into Northern Cyprus.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The share of the transport and communications industry in the GDP of Northern Cyprus is constantly varying; it decreased from 12.1% in 2008 to 8.5% in 2011, but rose again to 9.3% in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-secgdp_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-secgdp-107">[107]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Air transport is a major route of entry into Northern Cyprus. The country is home to two airports, the <a href="/wiki/Ercan_International_Airport" title="Ercan International Airport">Ercan International Airport</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ge%C3%A7itkale_Air_Base" title="Geçitkale Air Base">Geçitkale Airport</a>, of which only Ercan is currently functioning.<sup id="cite_ref-cypnet_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cypnet-118">[118]</a></sup> The Ercan airport saw an important renovation in the 2010s that greatly increased its passenger traffic, it was used by 1.76 million passengers in the first seven months of 2014 alone.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Non-stop flights are only available from multiple points in Turkey through a number of Turkish carriers.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Direct_flight" title="Direct flight">Direct</a> scheduled and <a href="/wiki/Charter_flight" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter flight">charter flights</a> take place from other countries, but with mandatory stopovers in Turkey. 600 charter flights were scheduled for 2013. Scheduled destinations include cities such as <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> while charter flight destinations include cities such as <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ljubljana" title="Ljubljana">Ljubljana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Direct flights to Northern Cyprus and the trade traffic through the Northern Cypriot ports are restricted as part of the embargo on Northern Cypriot ports.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The airports of <a href="/wiki/Ge%C3%A7itkale_airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Geçitkale airport">Geçitkale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ercan_airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Ercan airport">Ercan</a> are only recognised as legal ports of entry by Turkey and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Direct charter flights between <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> and North Cyprus started on 20 June 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The seaports in <a href="/wiki/Famagusta" title="Famagusta">Famagusta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kyrenia" title="Kyrenia">Kyrenia</a> have been declared closed to all shipping by the Republic of Cyprus since 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> By agreement between Northern Cyprus and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, there was a ship tour between Famagusta and <a href="/wiki/Latakia" title="Latakia">Latakia</a>, Syria before the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a>. Since the opening of the Green Line Turkish Cypriot residents are allowed to trade through ports recognized by the Republic of Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With the lack of a railway system, the country's highways are used for transport between major cities. In the 21st century, these highways were upgraded into <a href="/wiki/Dual_carriageway" title="Dual carriageway">dual carriageways</a>, with some roads in the Karpass area still being upgraded as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Northern_Cyprus&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. Northern Cyprus has around 7,000 kilometres (4,300 miles) of roads, with two thirds of these roads paved.<sup id="cite_ref-cypnet_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cypnet-118">[118]</a></sup> Recent constructions included the construction of a Northern Coast Highway, which was hailed as a major incentive for economic development.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black"> 
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:YellowGreen"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 5304.5364363156px; border-left-color:Silver"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Silver"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Silver"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 3978.035783976px; border-left-color:DarkGray"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DarkGray"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DarkGray"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 2651.3256287233px; border-left-color:DarkOrchid"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DarkOrchid"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DarkOrchid"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 1987.7609902728px; border-left-color:MediumSeaGreen"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:MediumSeaGreen"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:MediumSeaGreen"></div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Ethnic groups of Northern Cyprus (2006 census)<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> </p> 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:MediumSeaGreen; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a> (99.2%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:DarkOrchid; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a> (0.2%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:DarkGray; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a> (0.2%)

         <div class="legend">

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Cyprus" title="Demographics of Cyprus">Demographics of Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cypriots" title="Turkish Cypriots">Turkish Cypriots</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Turks_in_Northern_Cyprus" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainland Turks in Northern Cyprus">Mainland Turks in Northern Cyprus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Children_in_North_Nicosia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Children_in_North_Nicosia.jpg/220px-Children_in_North_Nicosia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Children_in_North_Nicosia.jpg/330px-Children_in_North_Nicosia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Children_in_North_Nicosia.jpg/440px-Children_in_North_Nicosia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4224" data-file-height="2376"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Children_in_North_Nicosia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Turkish Cypriot children in the walled part of North Nicosia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Northern Cyprus's first official census was performed in 1996. The population recorded was 200,587.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> The second census, carried out in 2006, revealed the population of Northern Cyprus to be 265,100,<sup id="cite_ref-census2006_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2006-132">[132]</a></sup> of which majority is composed of indigenous <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cypriots" title="Turkish Cypriots">Turkish Cypriots</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Cypriot_refugees" title="Cypriot refugees">refugees from Southern Cyprus</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Turks_in_Northern_Cyprus" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainland Turks in Northern Cyprus">settlers from Turkey</a>. Of the 178,000 Turkish Cypriot citizens, 82% are native Cypriots (145,000). Of the 45,000 people born to non-Cypriot parentage, nearly 40% (17,000) were born in Cyprus. The figure for non-citizens, including students, guest workers and temporary residents stood at 78,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-census2006_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2006-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The third official census of Northern Cyprus was carried out in 2011, made under the auspices of UN observers. It returned a total population of 294,906.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> These results were disputed by some political parties, labour unions and local newspapers. The government was accused of deliberately under-counting the population, after apparently giving an estimate of 700,000 before the census, in order to demand financial help from Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-censusDoubts_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censusDoubts-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-censusOverestimates_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censusOverestimates-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-census2011_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2011-137">[137]</a></sup> One source claims that the population in the north has reached 500,000,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> split between 50% Turkish Cypriots and 50% Turkish settlers or Cypriot-born children of such settlers.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Researcher Mete Hatay has written that such reports are "wildly speculative" and are picked up by opposition parties for political benefit, which resulted in reports in the south. Such reports have never been scientifically or statistically scrutinised, despite opportunities of opposition parties to do so using the electoral rolls in their possession, thereby continuing a "war of numbers".<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Government of Northern Cyprus estimates that the 1983 population of Northern Cyprus was 155,521.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> Estimates by the government of the <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Republic of Cyprus</a> from 2001 place the population at 200,000, of which 80–89,000 are Turkish Cypriots and 109,000–117,000 are designated as Turkish settlers by the Republic of Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-Euromosaic_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Euromosaic-142">[142]</a></sup> An island-wide census in 1960 indicated the number of Turkish Cypriots as 102,000 and Greek Cypriots as 450,000.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> As of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Northern_Cyprus&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the settlers constituted no more than 25% of the electorate in Northern Cyprus. The degree of the integration of mainland Turks to the Turkish Cypriot community varies; some identify as Turkish Cypriots and have culturally integrated, while some embrace a Turkish identity.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Northern Cyprus is almost entirely Turkish-speaking. English, however, is widely spoken as a second language.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>There are 644 <a href="/wiki/Greek_Cypriot" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Cypriot">Greek Cypriots</a> living in <a href="/wiki/Rizokarpaso" title="Rizokarpaso">Rizokarpaso</a> (Dipkarpaz) and 364 <a href="/wiki/Maronites" title="Maronites">Maronites</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kormakitis" title="Kormakitis">Kormakitis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> 162,000<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Greek Cypriots were forcibly evicted from their homes in the North by the invading force of the Turkish army.<sup id="cite_ref-Denver_journal_of_international_law_and_policy_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denver_journal_of_international_law_and_policy-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mallinson2011_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mallinson2011-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HörnerDöbert2006_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HörnerDöbert2006-149">[149]</a></sup> Rizokarpaso is the home of the biggest Greek-speaking population in the north. The Greek-Cypriot inhabitants are still supplied by the UN, and Greek-Cypriot products are consequently available in some shops.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p><br> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">
           <th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Northern Cyprus Religions<sup id="cite_ref-BoyleSheen2013_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BoyleSheen2013-150">[150]</a></sup></th>
          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;"></td>

           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:green; width:99%; overflow: hidden;">
