      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Cyprus" title="Religion in Cyprus">Religion in Cyprus</a>
      </div>
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Cyprus" title="Islam in Cyprus">Islam in Cyprus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Arabahmet_Mosque,_Nicosia,_Cyprus_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Arabahmet_Mosque%2C_Nicosia%2C_Cyprus_03.jpg/220px-Arabahmet_Mosque%2C_Nicosia%2C_Cyprus_03.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Arabahmet_Mosque%2C_Nicosia%2C_Cyprus_03.jpg/330px-Arabahmet_Mosque%2C_Nicosia%2C_Cyprus_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Arabahmet_Mosque%2C_Nicosia%2C_Cyprus_03.jpg/440px-Arabahmet_Mosque%2C_Nicosia%2C_Cyprus_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3352" data-file-height="3441"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Arabahmet_Mosque,_Nicosia,_Cyprus_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Arab_Ahmet_Mosque" title="Arab Ahmet Mosque">Arab Ahmet Mosque</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Nicosia" title="North Nicosia">North Nicosia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The majority of Turkish Cypriots (99%) are <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Muslims">Sunni Muslims</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BoyleSheen2013_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BoyleSheen2013-150">[150]</a></sup> Northern Cyprus is a secular state.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> Alcohol is frequently consumed within the community and most Turkish Cypriot women do not cover their heads; however headscarves are still worn on occasion by public figures as a symbol of the inhabitants' Turkish culture, or simply as a conservative form of dress.<sup id="cite_ref-BoyleSheen2013_150-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BoyleSheen2013-150">[150]</a></sup> However, some religious traditions still play a role within the community. Turkish Cypriot males are generally <a href="/wiki/Religious_male_circumcision" title="Religious male circumcision">circumcised</a> in accordance with religious beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Northern_Cyprus" title="Education in Northern Cyprus">Education in Northern Cyprus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Girne_Amerikan_%C3%9Cniversitesi_Kamp%C3%BCs.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Girne_Amerikan_%C3%9Cniversitesi_Kamp%C3%BCs.JPG/220px-Girne_Amerikan_%C3%9Cniversitesi_Kamp%C3%BCs.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Girne_Amerikan_%C3%9Cniversitesi_Kamp%C3%BCs.JPG/330px-Girne_Amerikan_%C3%9Cniversitesi_Kamp%C3%BCs.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Girne_Amerikan_%C3%9Cniversitesi_Kamp%C3%BCs.JPG/440px-Girne_Amerikan_%C3%9Cniversitesi_Kamp%C3%BCs.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Girne_Amerikan_%C3%9Cniversitesi_Kamp%C3%BCs.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Girne_American_University" title="Girne American University">Girne American University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kyrenia" title="Kyrenia">Kyrenia</a>, Northern Cyprus
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The education system in Northern Cyprus consists of pre-school education, primary education, secondary education and higher education. Five years of primary education is mandatory. </p>
      <p>Higher Education Planning Evaluation Accreditation and Coordination Council (YÖDAK) of Northern Cyprus is a member of International Network for Quality Assurance Agencies in Higher Education (INQAAHE).<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2013 there were 63,765 university students from 114 countries in nine universities in Northern Cyprus. In 2014, the number of students increased to 70,004, (15,210 Turkish Cypriots; 36,148 from Turkey; 18,646 international students):<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Near_East_University" title="Near East University">Near East University</a> (NEU),<sup id="cite_ref-neu.edu.tr_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neu.edu.tr-157">[157]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mastersportal.eu_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mastersportal.eu-158">[158]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Girne_American_University" title="Girne American University">Girne American University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Technical_University" title="Middle East Technical University">Middle East Technical University-TRNC</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_University_of_Lefke" title="European University of Lefke">European University of Lefke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_International_University" title="Cyprus International University">Cyprus International University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean_University" title="Eastern Mediterranean University">Eastern Mediterranean University</a> (EMU), <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Technical_University" title="Istanbul Technical University">Istanbul Technical University-TRNC</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mediterranean_Karpasia" title="University of Mediterranean Karpasia">University of Mediterranean Karpasia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kyrenia" title="University of Kyrenia">University of Kyrenia</a>, all established since 1974. EMU is an internationally recognised institution of higher learning with more than 1000 faculty members from 35 countries. There are 15,000 students in EMU representing 68 nationalities. The 8 universities have been approved by the Higher Education Council of Turkey. <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean_University" title="Eastern Mediterranean University">Eastern Mediterranean University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Near_East_University" title="Near East University">Near East University</a><sup id="cite_ref-neu.edu.tr_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neu.edu.tr-157">[157]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mastersportal.eu_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mastersportal.eu-158">[158]</a></sup> are full individual members of the <a href="/wiki/European_University_Association" title="European University Association">European University Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> EMU is a full member of the Community of Mediterranean Universities, Federation Universities of Islamic World, International Association of Universities and International Council of Graphic Design Associations,<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> and was ranked as the best university in the island and among the top 500 in Europe by <a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">Webometrics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Girne_American_University" title="Girne American University">Girne American University</a>, in the northern coastal city of <a href="/wiki/Kyrenia" title="Kyrenia">Kyrenia</a>, opened a campus in <a href="/wiki/Canterbury" title="Canterbury">Canterbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> and was accredited by the British Accreditation Council in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Northern Cyprus regularly participates in international Robocup competition, and took 14th place out of 20 in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> The country has supercomputers with which it participates in CERN experiments that led to the discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">Higgs boson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> Northern Cyprus is among participant countries of Solar Challenge of solar powered vehicles in South Africa in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Northern_Cyprus" title="Culture of Northern Cyprus">Culture of Northern Cyprus</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ziynet_Sali.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Ziynet_Sali.jpg/180px-Ziynet_Sali.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="270" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Ziynet_Sali.jpg/270px-Ziynet_Sali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Ziynet_Sali.jpg/360px-Ziynet_Sali.jpg 2x" data-file-width="683" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ziynet_Sali.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ziynet_Sali" title="Ziynet Sali">Ziynet Sali</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cypriot" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Cypriot">Turkish Cypriot</a> pop singer famous in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and Northern Cyprus.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Turkish_Cypriot_folk_dancers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Turkish_Cypriot_folk_dancers.jpg/220px-Turkish_Cypriot_folk_dancers.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Turkish_Cypriot_folk_dancers.jpg/330px-Turkish_Cypriot_folk_dancers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Turkish_Cypriot_folk_dancers.jpg/440px-Turkish_Cypriot_folk_dancers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="540"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Turkish_Cypriot_folk_dancers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cypriot" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Cypriot">Turkish Cypriot</a> children, dressed in traditional clothing, preparing for a folk-dance show
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cypriot_folk_dances" title="Turkish Cypriot folk dances">Turkish Cypriot folk dances</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Turkish Cypriot folk music consists of a rich variety of local tunes, influenced by the mainland Turkish music to a limited extent. Historically, it was shaped around the tradition of weddings, the primary social gatherings at the time. Violin, <a href="/wiki/Goblet_drum" title="Goblet drum">goblet drum</a>, known locally as "darbuka", <a href="/wiki/Zurna" title="Zurna">zurna</a> and other drums were heavily used in these gatherings, and a large number of traditional songs developed based on this legacy.<sup id="cite_ref-neukultur_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neukultur-168">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> Turkish Cypriot culture also incorporates a great diversity of folk dances with various influences, including different versions of <a href="/wiki/Karsilamas" title="Karsilamas">karsilamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%87iftetelli" class="mw-redirect" title="Çiftetelli">çiftetelli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zeybek_dance" title="Zeybek dance">zeybek</a>. </p>
      <p>The Northern Cyprus State Symphony Orchestra has been active since 1975. The <a href="/wiki/Bellapais_Abbey" title="Bellapais Abbey">Bellapais Abbey</a> in Kyrenia hosts international festivals of classical music, and is considered in important platform of classical music.<sup id="cite_ref-neukultur_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neukultur-168">[168]</a></sup> North Nicosia has its own Nicosia Municipal Orchestra that performs at open spaces, such as parks and squares, and is also home to the annual Walled City Jazz Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCya_Taner" title="Rüya Taner">Rüya Taner</a> is a Turkish Cypriot pianist who has achieved international acclaim. </p>
      <p>Turkish Cypriot cities and towns regularly organise festivals that include performances of local and international singers and bands.<sup id="cite_ref-neukultur_168-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neukultur-168">[168]</a></sup> Some Turkish Cypriot singers, such as <a href="/wiki/Ziynet_Sali" title="Ziynet Sali">Ziynet Sali</a> and <a href="/wiki/I%C5%9F%C4%B1n_Karaca" title="Işın Karaca">Işın Karaca</a>, have achieved fame in Turkey. The Turkish Cypriot band <a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C4%B1la_4&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sıla 4 (page does not exist)">Sıla 4</a> produced music that is considered essential for the Turkish Cypriot identity, and also acquired fame in Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> Rock and pop music are popular with the public in Northern Cyprus, important singers and bands include <a href="/wiki/SOS_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="SOS (band)">SOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fikri_Karayel" title="Fikri Karayel">Fikri Karayel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3> 
      <p>Poetry is the most widely published form of literature in Northern Cyprus. Turkish Cypriot poetry is based on both the effects of Turkish literature and the culture of the island of Cyprus, along with some reflection of the British colonial history.<sup id="cite_ref-siir_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-siir-174">[174]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first era of Turkish Cypriot poetry after the introduction of the Latin alphabet, characterised by poets such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nazif_S%C3%BCleyman_Ebeo%C4%9Flu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nazif Süleyman Ebeoğlu (page does not exist)">Nazif Süleyman Ebeoğlu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urkiye_Mine_Balman" title="Urkiye Mine Balman">Urkiye Mine Balman</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Engin_G%C3%B6n%C3%BCl&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Engin Gönül (page does not exist)">Engin Gönül</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Necla_Salih_Suphi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Necla Salih Suphi (page does not exist)">Necla Salih Suphi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pembe_Marmara" title="Pembe Marmara">Pembe Marmara</a>, had strong nationalistic elements due to the political attitudes of Turkish Cypriots at the time and stylistically reflected the poetry of the Turkish mainland. Meanwhile, other poets, such as <a href="/wiki/%C3%96zker_Ya%C5%9F%C4%B1n" title="Özker Yaşın">Özker Yaşın</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osman_T%C3%BCrkay" title="Osman Türkay">Osman Türkay</a>, who was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> twice,<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nevzat_Yal%C3%A7%C4%B1n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nevzat Yalçın (page does not exist)">Nevzat Yalçın</a> sought to write in more original styles, with the influence of nascent poetic styles in Turkey and those in Britain. This group of poets were very prolific and increased the popularity of poetry in the Turkish Cypriot community, and are seen as key figures in Turkish Cypriot literature.<sup id="cite_ref-siir_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-siir-174">[174]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The nationalism gave way to a notion of Cypriotness in the 1970s, with the influence of Yaşın, Türkay and Yalçın. During this period, the so-called "1974 generation of poets" arose, led by poets including <a href="/wiki/Mehmet_Ya%C5%9F%C4%B1n" title="Mehmet Yaşın">Mehmet Yaşın</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hakk%C4%B1_Y%C3%BCcel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hakkı Yücel (page does not exist)">Hakkı Yücel</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nice_Denizo%C4%9Flu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nice Denizoğlu (page does not exist)">Nice Denizoğlu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ne%C5%9Fe_Ya%C5%9F%C4%B1n" title="Neşe Yaşın">Neşe Yaşın</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ay%C5%9Fen_Da%C4%9Fl%C4%B1&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ayşen Dağlı (page does not exist)">Ayşen Dağlı</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Canan_S%C3%BCmer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Canan Sümer (page does not exist)">Canan Sümer</a>. The poetry of this generation was characterised by the appreciation of the Turkish Cypriot identity as distinct from Turkish identity and the identification of Cyprus as the Turkish Cypriot homeland instead of Turkey, in contrast to the previous nationalist poetry. This approach is often called the "Cypriot poetry of rejection" as it resists the influence of Turkey, highlighting the cultural rift between Turkey and Cyprus due to the recent experience of war and therefore the independence of the Turkish Cypriot poetry and identity. This was followed by an increased adoption of the Mediterranean identity in the 1980s, accompanied by the effects of the liberalisation of the Turkish Cypriot society, as reflected in the feminist elements, of which a particular example is <a href="/wiki/Neriman_Cahit" title="Neriman Cahit">Neriman Cahit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-siir_174-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-siir-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3> 
      <p><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anahtar_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Anahtar (film) (page does not exist)">Anahtar</a></i> (<i>Key</i>), released in 2011, was the first full-length film entirely produced in Northern Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Some other co-productions have also taken place. A co-production of Northern Cyprus, Turkey, Britain and the Netherlands, <i><a href="https://tr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kod_Ad%C4%B1_Ven%C3%BCs" class="extiw" title="tr:Kod Adı Venüs">Kod Adı Venüs</a><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></i> (<i>Code Name Venus</i>) was shown in the <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a> in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> The film director and screenwriter <a href="/wiki/Dervi%C5%9F_Zaim" title="Derviş Zaim">Derviş Zaim</a> achieved fame with his 2003 film <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mud_(%C3%87amur)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mud (Çamur) (page does not exist)">Mud (Çamur)</a></i> which won the UNESCO award at the <a href="/wiki/Venice_Film_Festival" title="Venice Film Festival">Venice Film Festival</a>. </p>
      <p>The documentary film <i>Kayıp Otobüs</i> (<i><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Missing_Bus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Missing Bus (page does not exist)">The Missing Bus</a></i>), directed by Turkish Cypriot journalist Fevzi Tașpınar, was aired on the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Radio_and_Television_Corporation" title="Turkish Radio and Television Corporation">TRT TV</a> as well as participating in the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Film_Festival" title="Boston Film Festival">Boston Film Festival</a> in 2011. The film tells the story of eleven Turkish Cypriot workers who left their homes in a bus in 1964 that never came back. Their remains were found in a well in Cyprus in October 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre">Theatre</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Karagoez-davul-Hacivat-zurna.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Karagoez-davul-Hacivat-zurna.jpg/220px-Karagoez-davul-Hacivat-zurna.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5b/Karagoez-davul-Hacivat-zurna.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="322" data-file-height="281"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Karagoez-davul-Hacivat-zurna.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Karag%C3%B6z_and_Hacivat" title="Karagöz and Hacivat">Karagöz and Hacivat</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:An_early_Turkish-Cypriot_theatre_group.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/An_early_Turkish-Cypriot_theatre_group.jpg/220px-An_early_Turkish-Cypriot_theatre_group.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a9/An_early_Turkish-Cypriot_theatre_group.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="285" data-file-height="182"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:An_early_Turkish-Cypriot_theatre_group.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An early <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cypriot" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Cypriot">Turkish Cypriot</a> theatre group, 1880s
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Theatre in Northern Cyprus is mostly carried out by the Turkish Cypriot State Theatre, municipal theatres and a number of private theatrical companies. Cyprus Theatre Festival, organised by the <a href="/wiki/Nicosia_Turkish_Municipality" title="Nicosia Turkish Municipality">Nicosia Turkish Municipality</a> is a large organisation with institutions from Turkey participating as well. There are no major halls built specifically for theatre in Northern Cyprus, so plays often take place in conference halls.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The origins of Turkish Cypriot theatre lie in <a href="/wiki/Karag%C3%B6z_and_Hacivat" title="Karagöz and Hacivat">Karagöz and Hacivat</a>, a shadow play that was popularised in the island as a form of entertainment during the Ottoman era. This form of theatre has lost its popularity nowadays, but remains to be televised during religious festivals.<sup id="cite_ref-cypnetth_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cypnetth-185">[185]</a></sup> After the 1840s, as the Ottoman Empire started modernising, theatre with greater European elements met with the Turkish Cypriot public. However, the inception of Turkish Cypriot theatre in the modern sense is considered the staging of the play "Vatan Yahut Silistre" ("Homeland vs. Silistra") by Turkish playwright <a href="/wiki/Nam%C4%B1k_Kemal" title="Namık Kemal">Namık Kemal</a> in 1908.<sup id="cite_ref-turkth_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turkth-186">[186]</a></sup> This was followed by a proliferation of theatrical activity in the Turkish Cypriot community as local plays were written and staged and theatrical companies from Turkey took the stage in Cyprus by the 1920s, all the major towns in Cyprus had Turkish Cypriot plays that were performed regularly.<sup id="cite_ref-cypnetth_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cypnetth-185">[185]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-turkth_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turkth-186">[186]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 1960s, Turkish Cypriot theatre started to be institutionalised. A leading theatre group named "İlk Sahne" (First Stage), founded in 1963, was renamed the Turkish Cypriot State Theatre in 1966, and has since performed more than 85 plays.<sup id="cite_ref-cypnetth_185-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cypnetth-185">[185]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> Theatre is currently a very popular form of art in Northern Cyprus, with long queues forming for tickets of the plays in the Cyprus Theatre Festival, and the number of theatre-goers constantly increasing.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Northern_Cyprus" title="Sport in Northern Cyprus">Sport in Northern Cyprus</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nicosia_Ataturk_Stadium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Nicosia_Ataturk_Stadium.jpg/220px-Nicosia_Ataturk_Stadium.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Nicosia_Ataturk_Stadium.jpg/330px-Nicosia_Ataturk_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Nicosia_Ataturk_Stadium.jpg/440px-Nicosia_Ataturk_Stadium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nicosia_Ataturk_Stadium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Nicosia_Atat%C3%BCrk_Stadium" title="Nicosia Atatürk Stadium">Nicosia Atatürk Stadium</a> is the largest stadium in Northern Cyprus.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are five stadiums in Northern Cyprus, with each holding a capacity ranging anywhere from 7,000 to 30,000. The most popular sport in Northern Cyprus is football. There are over 29 sport federations in Northern Cyprus with a total registered membership of 13,950 6,054 been registered practitioners for, <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">taekwondo</a>-<a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">karate</a>-<a href="/wiki/Aikido" title="Aikido">aikido</a>-<a href="/wiki/Kurash" title="Kurash">kurash</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Shooting" title="Shooting">shooting</a> having 1,150 (registered) and <a href="/wiki/Hunting" title="Hunting">hunting</a> having 1,017 (registered) members.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> Northern Cyprus' <a href="/wiki/Northern_Cyprus_national_football_team" title="Northern Cyprus national football team">national football team</a> currently ranks 109th in the Elo Ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> Several of sport clubs participate in leagues in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. These include the Fast Break Sport Club in Turkey's Men's Basketball Regional League; the Beşparmak Sport Club in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>'s Handball Premier League; and the <a href="/wiki/Lefke_European_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Lefke European University">Lefke European University</a> <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> Table-tennis Super League. Water sports such as windsurfing, jetskiing, waterskiing and sailing are also available at beaches throughout the coastline of Northern Cyprus. Sailing is especially found at Escape Beach Club, near <a href="/wiki/Kyrenia" title="Kyrenia">Kyrenia</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <p>Northern Cyprus is also well known for several dishes; among them are kebabs made of skewered lamb (şiş kebab) or ground with herbs and spices and made into a <a href="/wiki/Kofte" class="mw-redirect" title="Kofte">kofte</a> or şeftali kebab. Other dishes are based on meat wrapped in flat bread such as <a href="/wiki/Lahmacun" title="Lahmacun">lahmacun</a>. Vegetarian cuisine includes stuffed vegetable based dishes "yalancı dolma" or many other dishes made with a bean or pulse such as börülce which consists of Swiss chard cooked with black-eyed peas. There are also plant based foods such as <a href="/wiki/Molohiya" class="mw-redirect" title="Molohiya">molohiya</a> or root based stews such as kolokas.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> </p>
